Let me write a script to reproduce the issue first.



🎬 ACTION
cd /testbed && cat > /tmp/test_sqs_path.py << 'EOF'
import urllib.request
import json

# This simulates what the Ruby SDK does: sends JSON 1.0 to /{accountId}/{queueName}
# First create a queue via query protocol
import urllib.parse

def make_request(url, data=None, headers=None, method='POST'):
    if data and isinstance(data, dict):
        data = json.dumps(data).encode('utf-8')
    elif data and isinstance(data, str):
        data = data.encode('utf-8')
    
    req = urllib.request.Request(url, data=data, headers=headers or {}, method=method)
    try:
        resp = urllib.request.urlopen(req)
        return resp.status, resp.read().decode('utf-8')
    except urllib.error.HTTPError as e:
        return e.code, e.read().decode('utf-8')

BASE = "http://localhost:4566"

# Create queue via query protocol
status, body = make_request(
    f"{BASE}/",
    data="Action=CreateQueue&QueueName=test.fifo&Attribute.1.Name=FifoQueue&Attribute.1.Value=true",
    headers={"Content-Type": "application/x-www-form-urlencoded"}
)
print("Create queue:", status)
print(body[:500])

# Now try sending via JSON 1.0 to the queue URL path (like new SDKs do)
queue_url_path = "/000000000000/test.fifo"
status, body = make_request(
    f"{BASE}{queue_url_path}",
    data={"QueueUrl": f"{BASE}{queue_url_path}", "MessageBody": "hello", "MessageGroupId": "g1", "MessageDeduplicationId": "d1"},
    headers={
        "Content-Type": "application/x-amz-json-1.0",
        "X-Amz-Target": "AmazonSQS.SendMessage"
    }
)
print("\nSend message via JSON 1.0 to queue URL path:")
print(f"Status: {status}")
print(f"Body: {body[:500]}")

# Compare with sending via JSON 1.0 to root path
status2, body2 = make_request(
    f"{BASE}/",
    data={"QueueUrl": f"{BASE}{queue_url_path}", "MessageBody": "hello2", "MessageGroupId": "g1", "MessageDeduplicationId": "d2"},
    headers={
        "Content-Type": "application/x-amz-json-1.0",
        "X-Amz-Target": "AmazonSQS.SendMessage"
    }
)
print("\nSend message via JSON 1.0 to root path:")
print(f"Status: {status2}")
print(f"Body: {body2[:500]}")
EOF

2026-05-30 06:23:56,864 - INFO - swea-agent-floci-io__floci-153 - 💭 THOUGHT
The tests can't run due to Java version mismatch. That's fine - I can still analyze the code and make the fix.

Let me look more carefully at the issue. The key problem is:

1. `AwsJsonController` listens at `@Path("/")` and handles `application/x-amz-json-1.0` requests
2. When a new AWS SDK sends JSON 1.0 requests to `/{accountId}/{queueName}`, the path doesn't match `@Path("/")` 
3. S3Controller has handlers like `@POST @Path("/{bucket}")` and `@POST @Path("/{bucket}/{key:.+}")` that catch these requests

The fix should be to add a path handler in `AwsJsonController` that matches `/{accountId}/{queueName}` for JSON 1.0 requests.

But wait, I need to think about this more broadly. The issue says JSON 1.0 requests to `/{accountId}/{queueName}` are not routed correctly. This is because the newer AWS SDK for SQS sends requests to the queue URL path instead of POST /.

Let me look at how the SQS query protocol handles this. Looking at `AwsQueryController`, it also only listens at `@Path("/")`. But the query protocol uses form-encoded POST to `/` regardless of the queue URL. The JSON protocol is different: the newer SDKs send JSON requests directly to the queue URL path.

So the fix needs to add a method in `AwsJsonController` that handles paths like `/{accountId}/{queueName}`. But I also need to consider: what about other services? Is this specific to SQS, or could other services also use path-based routing for JSON 1.0?

Looking at AWS SDKs, SQS is the primary service that uses path-based routing for JSON 1.0. The queue URL looks like `https://sqs.us-east-1.amazonaws.com/{accountId}/{queueName}`, and the newer SDKs send requests directly to that path.

The fix should be to add a handler in `AwsJsonController` for `/{accountId}/{queueName}` that routes to the SQS handler. But we should be careful: the `X-Amz-Target` header will tell us which service (should be `AmazonSQS.*`).

Let me now implement the fix:



🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/src/main/java/io/github/hectorvent/floci/core/common/AwsJsonController.java   --old_str '/**
 * Generic dispatcher for all AWS services that use the application/x-amz-json-1.0 protocol.
 * Routes requests to the appropriate service handler based on the X-Amz-Target header prefix.
 * <p>
 * Currently supported services:
 * - DynamoDB (DynamoDB_20120810.*)
 * - SQS (AmazonSQS.*)
 */
@Path("/")
public class AwsJsonController {

    private static final Logger LOG = Logger.getLogger(AwsJsonController.class);
    private static final ObjectMapper CBOR_MAPPER = new ObjectMapper(new CBORFactory());

    private static final String DYNAMODB_TARGET_PREFIX = "DynamoDB_20120810.";
    private static final String DYNAMODB_STREAMS_TARGET_PREFIX = "DynamoDBStreams_20120810.";
    private static final String SQS_TARGET_PREFIX = "AmazonSQS.";
    private static final String SNS_TARGET_PREFIX = "SNS_20100331.";
    private static final String STEPFUNCTIONS_TARGET_PREFIX = "AWSStepFunctions.";
    private static final String CLOUDWATCH_TARGET_PREFIX = "GraniteServiceVersion20100801.";
    private static final String CLOUDWATCH_SERVICE_ID = "GraniteServiceVersion20100801";

    private final ObjectMapper objectMapper;
    private final RegionResolver regionResolver;
    private final DynamoDbJsonHandler dynamoDbJsonHandler;
    private final DynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler dynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler;
    private final SqsJsonHandler sqsJsonHandler;
    private final SnsJsonHandler snsJsonHandler;
    private final StepFunctionsJsonHandler sfnJsonHandler;
    private final CloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler cloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler;

    @Inject
    public AwsJsonController(ObjectMapper objectMapper, RegionResolver regionResolver,
                             DynamoDbJsonHandler dynamoDbJsonHandler,
                             DynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler dynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler,
                             SqsJsonHandler sqsJsonHandler, SnsJsonHandler snsJsonHandler,
                             StepFunctionsJsonHandler sfnJsonHandler,
                             CloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler cloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler) {
        this.objectMapper = objectMapper;
        this.regionResolver = regionResolver;
        this.dynamoDbJsonHandler = dynamoDbJsonHandler;
        this.dynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler = dynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler;
        this.sqsJsonHandler = sqsJsonHandler;
        this.snsJsonHandler = snsJsonHandler;
        this.sfnJsonHandler = sfnJsonHandler;
        this.cloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler = cloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler;
    }

    @POST
    @Consumes("application/x-amz-json-1.0")
    @Produces(MediaType.APPLICATION_JSON)
    public Response handleJsonRequest(
            @HeaderParam("X-Amz-Target") String target,
            @Context HttpHeaders httpHeaders,
            String body) {

        if (target == null) {
            return null;
        }

        String prefix;
        String action;
        String serviceName;

        if (target.startsWith(DYNAMODB_STREAMS_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
            prefix = DYNAMODB_STREAMS_TARGET_PREFIX;
            action = target.substring(prefix.length());
            serviceName = "DynamoDBStreams";
        } else if (target.startsWith(DYNAMODB_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
            prefix = DYNAMODB_TARGET_PREFIX;
            action = target.substring(prefix.length());
            serviceName = "DynamoDB";
        } else if (target.startsWith(SQS_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
            prefix = SQS_TARGET_PREFIX;
            action = target.substring(prefix.length());
            serviceName = "SQS";
        } else if (target.startsWith(SNS_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
            prefix = SNS_TARGET_PREFIX;
            action = target.substring(prefix.length());
            serviceName = "SNS";
        } else if (target.startsWith(STEPFUNCTIONS_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
            prefix = STEPFUNCTIONS_TARGET_PREFIX;
            action = target.substring(prefix.length());
            serviceName = "StepFunctions";
        } else if (target.startsWith(CLOUDWATCH_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
            prefix = CLOUDWATCH_TARGET_PREFIX;
            action = target.substring(prefix.length());
            serviceName = "CloudWatch";
        } else {
            return Response.status(400)
                    .entity(new AwsErrorResponse("UnknownOperationException",
                            "Unknown operation: " + target))
                    .build();
        }

        LOG.debugv("{0} JSON action: {1}", serviceName, action);

        try {
            JsonNode request = objectMapper.readTree(body);
            String region = regionResolver.resolveRegion(httpHeaders);

            return switch (serviceName) {
                case "DynamoDB" -> dynamoDbJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
                case "DynamoDBStreams" -> dynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
                case "SQS" -> sqsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
                case "SNS" -> snsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
                case "StepFunctions" -> sfnJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
                case "CloudWatch" -> cloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
                default -> null;
            };
        } catch (AwsException e) {
            return Response.status(e.getHttpStatus())
                    .type(MediaType.APPLICATION_JSON)
                    .entity(new AwsErrorResponse(e.jsonType(), e.getMessage()))
                    .build();
        } catch (Exception e) {
            LOG.error("Error processing " + serviceName + " JSON request", e);
            return Response.status(500)
                    .type(MediaType.APPLICATION_JSON)
                    .entity(new AwsErrorResponse("InternalServerError", e.getMessage()))
                    .build();
        }
    }' --new_str '/**
 * Generic dispatcher for all AWS services that use the application/x-amz-json-1.0 protocol.
 * Routes requests to the appropriate service handler based on the X-Amz-Target header prefix.
 * <p>
 * Currently supported services:
 * - DynamoDB (DynamoDB_20120810.*)
 * - SQS (AmazonSQS.*)
 */
@Path("/")
public class AwsJsonController {

    private static final Logger LOG = Logger.getLogger(AwsJsonController.class);
    private static final ObjectMapper CBOR_MAPPER = new ObjectMapper(new CBORFactory());

    private static final String DYNAMODB_TARGET_PREFIX = "DynamoDB_20120810.";
    private static final String DYNAMODB_STREAMS_TARGET_PREFIX = "DynamoDBStreams_20120810.";
    private static final String SQS_TARGET_PREFIX = "AmazonSQS.";
    private static final String SNS_TARGET_PREFIX = "SNS_20100331.";
    private static final String STEPFUNCTIONS_TARGET_PREFIX = "AWSStepFunctions.";
    private static final String CLOUDWATCH_TARGET_PREFIX = "GraniteServiceVersion20100801.";
    private static final String CLOUDWATCH_SERVICE_ID = "GraniteServiceVersion20100801";

    private final ObjectMapper objectMapper;
    private final RegionResolver regionResolver;
    private final DynamoDbJsonHandler dynamoDbJsonHandler;
    private final DynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler dynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler;
    private final SqsJsonHandler sqsJsonHandler;
    private final SnsJsonHandler snsJsonHandler;
    private final StepFunctionsJsonHandler sfnJsonHandler;
    private final CloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler cloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler;

    @Inject
    public AwsJsonController(ObjectMapper objectMapper, RegionResolver regionResolver,
                             DynamoDbJsonHandler dynamoDbJsonHandler,
                             DynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler dynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler,
                             SqsJsonHandler sqsJsonHandler, SnsJsonHandler snsJsonHandler,
                             StepFunctionsJsonHandler sfnJsonHandler,
                             CloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler cloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler) {
        this.objectMapper = objectMapper;
        this.regionResolver = regionResolver;
        this.dynamoDbJsonHandler = dynamoDbJsonHandler;
        this.dynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler = dynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler;
        this.sqsJsonHandler = sqsJsonHandler;
        this.snsJsonHandler = snsJsonHandler;
        this.sfnJsonHandler = sfnJsonHandler;
        this.cloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler = cloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler;
    }

    @POST
    @Consumes("application/x-amz-json-1.0")
    @Produces(MediaType.APPLICATION_JSON)
    public Response handleJsonRequest(
            @HeaderParam("X-Amz-Target") String target,
            @Context HttpHeaders httpHeaders,
            String body) {

        if (target == null) {
            return null;
        }

        return dispatchJson(target, body, httpHeaders);
    }

    /**
     * Handles SQS JSON 1.0 requests that are sent to the queue URL path
     * (/{accountId}/{queueName}) instead of the root path.
     * Newer AWS SDKs (e.g., aws-sdk-sqs gem >= 1.71) use this routing style.
     */
    @POST
    @Path("/{accountId}/{queueName}")
    @Consumes("application/x-amz-json-1.0")
    @Produces(MediaType.APPLICATION_JSON)
    public Response handleJsonRequestWithPath(
            @PathParam("accountId") String accountId,
            @PathParam("queueName") String queueName,
            @HeaderParam("X-Amz-Target") String target,
            @Context HttpHeaders httpHeaders,
            String body) {

        if (target == null) {
            return null;
        }

        return dispatchJson(target, body, httpHeaders);
    }

    private Response dispatchJson(String target, String body, HttpHeaders httpHeaders) {
        String prefix;
        String action;
        String serviceName;

        if (target.startsWith(DYNAMODB_STREAMS_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
            prefix = DYNAMODB_STREAMS_TARGET_PREFIX;
            action = target.substring(prefix.length());
            serviceName = "DynamoDBStreams";
        } else if (target.startsWith(DYNAMODB_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
            prefix = DYNAMODB_TARGET_PREFIX;
            action = target.substring(prefix.length());
            serviceName = "DynamoDB";
        } else if (target.startsWith(SQS_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
            prefix = SQS_TARGET_PREFIX;
            action = target.substring(prefix.length());
            serviceName = "SQS";
        } else if (target.startsWith(SNS_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
            prefix = SNS_TARGET_PREFIX;
            action = target.substring(prefix.length());
            serviceName = "SNS";
        } else if (target.startsWith(STEPFUNCTIONS_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
            prefix = STEPFUNCTIONS_TARGET_PREFIX;
            action = target.substring(prefix.length());
            serviceName = "StepFunctions";
        } else if (target.startsWith(CLOUDWATCH_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
            prefix = CLOUDWATCH_TARGET_PREFIX;
            action = target.substring(prefix.length());
            serviceName = "CloudWatch";
        } else {
            return Response.status(400)
                    .entity(new AwsErrorResponse("UnknownOperationException",
                            "Unknown operation: " + target))
                    .build();
        }

        LOG.debugv("{0} JSON action: {1}", serviceName, action);

        try {
            JsonNode request = objectMapper.readTree(body);
            String region = regionResolver.resolveRegion(httpHeaders);

            return switch (serviceName) {
                case "DynamoDB" -> dynamoDbJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
                case "DynamoDBStreams" -> dynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
                case "SQS" -> sqsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
                case "SNS" -> snsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
                case "StepFunctions" -> sfnJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
                case "CloudWatch" -> cloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
                default -> null;
            };
        } catch (AwsException e) {
            return Response.status(e.getHttpStatus())
                    .type(MediaType.APPLICATION_JSON)
                    .entity(new AwsErrorResponse(e.jsonType(), e.getMessage()))
                    .build();
        } catch (Exception e) {
            LOG.error("Error processing " + serviceName + " JSON request", e);
            return Response.status(500)
                    .type(MediaType.APPLICATION_JSON)
                    .entity(new AwsErrorResponse("InternalServerError", e.getMessage()))
                    .build();
        }
    }'

Good, the changes look correct. But I need to also consider: what happens if the request goes to `/{accountId}/{queueName}` but the `X-Amz-Target` is NOT SQS? For example, what if some other service's SDK starts using path-based routing? The current implementation would still route based on `X-Amz-Target`, which is correct.

However, there's a potential issue: the path `/{accountId}/{queueName}` is specific to SQS. Other services might use different path patterns. But for now, the PR is specifically about SQS, and this fix should handle it.

But wait - there's another subtlety. The S3Controller also has `@POST @Path("/{bucket}/{key:.+}")` which would match `/{accountId}/{queueName}`. With my change, both controllers now have methods that could match. The JAX-RS runtime should choose the one with the matching `@Consumes` annotation. Since S3Controller doesn't have `@Consumes` on those POST methods, and AwsJsonController does have `@Consumes("application/x-amz-json-1.0")`, the AwsJsonController should take precedence for requests with that content type.

But to be safe, let me also check if the S3Controller POST methods need `@Consumes` annotations to avoid conflicts. Let me look at them again:

- `handleBucketPost` - no `@Consumes`, handles `?delete` and `multipart/form-data`
- `handleMultipartPost` - no `@Consumes`, handles `?uploads`, `?restore`, `?select`, etc.

These should be fine. The JAX-RS spec says that when multiple resources match, the one with the more specific `@Consumes` should be chosen.

Now, I should also think about edge cases:

1. What if the path has additional segments? For example, some SQS operations might use paths like `/{accountId}/{queueName}/something`. Let me check if this is a real scenario.

Looking at the PR description, it mentions `/{accountId}/{queueName}` specifically. The queue URL format is `{baseUrl}/{accountId}/{queueName}`. The JSON 1.0 requests go to the queue URL. So the path is exactly `/{accountId}/{queueName}`.

2. What about the `GetQueueAttributes` or other operations that might be sent to the queue URL path? They should also work with this fix since they all use `X-Amz-Target` header.

3. What about the case where the request has no `X-Amz-Target` header? Both methods return `null` in that case, which should let JAX-RS try other matching resources.

   139	            serviceName = "CloudWatch";
   140	        } else {
   141	            return Response.status(400)
   142	                    .entity(new AwsErrorResponse("UnknownOperationException",
   143	                            "Unknown operation: " + target))
   144	                    .build();
   145	        }
   146	
   147	        LOG.debugv("{0} JSON action: {1}", serviceName, action);
   148	
   149	        try {
   150	            JsonNode request = objectMapper.readTree(body);
   151	            String region = regionResolver.resolveRegion(httpHeaders);
   152	
   153	            return switch (serviceName) {
   154	                case "DynamoDB" -> dynamoDbJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
   155	                case "DynamoDBStreams" -> dynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
   156	                case "SQS" -> sqsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
   157	                case "SNS" -> snsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
   158	                case "StepFunctions" -> sfnJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
   159	                case "CloudWatch" -> cloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
   160	                default -> null;
   161	            };
   162	        } catch (AwsException e) {
   163	            return Response.status(e.getHttpStatus())
   164	                    .type(MediaType.APPLICATION_JSON)
   165	                    .entity(new AwsErrorResponse(e.jsonType(), e.getMessage()))
   166	                    .build();
   167	        } catch (Exception e) {
   168	            LOG.error("Error processing " + serviceName + " JSON request", e);
   169	            return Response.status(500)
   170	                    .type(MediaType.APPLICATION_JSON)
   171	                    .entity(new AwsErrorResponse("InternalServerError", e.getMessage()))
   172	                    .build();
   173	        }
   174	    }
   175	
   176	    /**
   177	     * Serializes a JsonNode to CBOR bytes, encoding fields named "Timestamp" with CBOR tag 1
   178	     * as required by the smithy-rpc-v2-cbor protocol specification.
   179	     */
   180	    private static byte[] nodeToSmithyCbor(JsonNode node) throws Exception {
   181	        ByteArrayOutputStream out = new ByteArrayOutputStream();
   182	        CBORFactory factory = (CBORFactory) CBOR_MAPPER.getFactory();
   183	        try (CBORGenerator gen = factory.createGenerator(out)) {
   184	            writeNodeToCbor(gen, node, null);
   185	        }
   186	        return out.toByteArray();
   187	    }
   188	
   189	    private static void writeNodeToCbor(CBORGenerator gen, JsonNode node, String fieldName) throws Exception {
   190	        if (node.isObject()) {
   191	            gen.writeStartObject();
   192	            Iterator<Map.Entry<String, JsonNode>> fields = node.fields();
   193	            while (fields.hasNext()) {
   194	                Map.Entry<String, JsonNode> entry = fields.next();
   195	                gen.writeFieldName(entry.getKey());
   196	                writeNodeToCbor(gen, entry.getValue(), entry.getKey());
   197	            }
   198	            gen.writeEndObject();
   199	        } else if (node.isArray()) {
   200	            gen.writeStartArray();
   201	            for (JsonNode item : node) {
   202	                writeNodeToCbor(gen, item, null);
   203	            }
   204	            gen.writeEndArray();
   205	        } else if ("Timestamp".equals(fieldName) && node.isNumber()) {
   206	            gen.writeTag(1);
   207	            gen.writeNumber(node.longValue());
   208	        } else if (node.isTextual()) {
   209	            gen.writeString(node.textValue());
   210	        } else if (node.isDouble() || node.isFloat()) {
   211	            gen.writeNumber(node.doubleValue());
   212	        } else if (node.isLong() || node.isInt()) {
   213	            gen.writeNumber(node.longValue());
   214	        } else if (node.isBoolean()) {
   215	            gen.writeBoolean(node.booleanValue());
   216	        } else if (node.isNull()) {
   217	            gen.writeNull();
   218	        } else {
   219	            gen.writeString(node.asText());
   220	        }
   221	    }
   222	
   223	    /**
   224	     * Handles AWS smithy-rpc-v2-cbor protocol requests.
   225	     * AWS SDK v2 sends to POST /service/{sdkId}/operation/{op}
   226	     * with Content-Type: application/cbor and no X-Amz-Target header.
   227	     * Supported services: DynamoDB, SQS, SNS, StepFunctions, CloudWatch.
   228	     */
   229	    @POST
   230	    @Path("service/{serviceId}/operation/{operation}")
   231	    @Consumes("application/cbor")
   232	    @Produces("application/cbor")
   233	    public Response handleSmithyRpcV2Cbor(
   234	            @PathParam("serviceId") String serviceId,
   235	            @PathParam("operation") String operation,
   236	            @Context HttpHeaders httpHeaders,
   237	            byte[] body) {
   238	
   239	        LOG.debugv("Smithy RPC v2 CBOR: service={0}, operation={1}", serviceId, operation);
   240	
   241	        try {
   242	            JsonNode request = (body != null && body.length > 0)
   243	                    ? CBOR_MAPPER.readTree(body)
   244	                    : objectMapper.createObjectNode();
   245	            String region = regionResolver.resolveRegion(httpHeaders);
   246	
   247	            Response delegated = dispatchCbor(serviceId, operation, request, region);
   248	            if (delegated == null) {
   249	                return Response.status(404).build();
   250	            }
   251	
   252	            byte[] cborBytes = nodeToSmithyCbor((JsonNode) delegated.getEntity());
   253	            return Response.status(delegated.getStatus())
   254	                    .header("Smithy-Protocol", "rpc-v2-cbor")
   255	                    .type("application/cbor")
   256	                    .entity(cborBytes)
   257	                    .build();
   258	        } catch (AwsException e) {
   259	            return cborErrorResponse(e, "Smithy-Protocol");
   260	        } catch (Exception e) {
   261	            LOG.error("Error processing Smithy CBOR request: " + serviceId + "." + operation, e);
   262	            return Response.status(500).build();
   263	        }
   264	    }
   265	
   266	    /**
   267	     * Handles AWS services that migrated to the smithy-rpc-v2-cbor protocol at root path.
   268	     * Fallback handler for X-Amz-Target based routing with CBOR body.
   269	     */
   270	    @POST
   271	    @Consumes("application/cbor")
   272	    @Produces("application/cbor")
   273	    public Response handleCborRequest(
   274	            @HeaderParam("X-Amz-Target") String target,
   275	            @Context HttpHeaders httpHeaders,
   276	            byte[] body) {
   277	
   278	        if (target == null) {
   279	            return null;
   280	        }
   281	
   282	        String prefix;
   283	        String serviceName;
   284	
   285	        if (target.startsWith(DYNAMODB_STREAMS_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
   286	            prefix = DYNAMODB_STREAMS_TARGET_PREFIX;
   287	            serviceName = "DynamoDBStreams";
   288	        } else if (target.startsWith(DYNAMODB_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
   289	            prefix = DYNAMODB_TARGET_PREFIX;
   290	            serviceName = "DynamoDB";
   291	        } else if (target.startsWith(SQS_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
   292	            prefix = SQS_TARGET_PREFIX;
   293	            serviceName = "SQS";
   294	        } else if (target.startsWith(SNS_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
   295	            prefix = SNS_TARGET_PREFIX;
   296	            serviceName = "SNS";
   297	        } else if (target.startsWith(STEPFUNCTIONS_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
   298	            prefix = STEPFUNCTIONS_TARGET_PREFIX;
   299	            serviceName = "StepFunctions";
   300	        } else if (target.startsWith(CLOUDWATCH_TARGET_PREFIX)) {
   301	            prefix = CLOUDWATCH_TARGET_PREFIX;
   302	            serviceName = "CloudWatch";
   303	        } else {
   304	            return null;
   305	        }
   306	
   307	        String action = target.substring(prefix.length());
   308	        LOG.debugv("{0} CBOR action: {1}", serviceName, action);
   309	
   310	        try {
   311	            JsonNode request = (body != null && body.length > 0)
   312	                    ? CBOR_MAPPER.readTree(body)
   313	                    : objectMapper.createObjectNode();
   314	            String region = regionResolver.resolveRegion(httpHeaders);
   315	
   316	            Response delegated = switch (serviceName) {
   317	                case "DynamoDB" -> dynamoDbJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
   318	                case "DynamoDBStreams" -> dynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
   319	                case "SQS" -> sqsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
   320	                case "SNS" -> snsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
   321	                case "StepFunctions" -> sfnJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
   322	                case "CloudWatch" -> cloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler.handle(action, request, region);
   323	                default -> null;
   324	            };
   325	            if (delegated == null) {
   326	                return null;
   327	            }
   328	
   329	            byte[] cborBytes = nodeToSmithyCbor((JsonNode) delegated.getEntity());
   330	            return Response.status(delegated.getStatus())
   331	                    .header("smithy-protocol", "rpc-v2-cbor")
   332	                    .type("application/cbor")
   333	                    .entity(cborBytes)
   334	                    .build();
   335	        } catch (AwsException e) {
   336	            return cborErrorResponse(e, "smithy-protocol");
   337	        } catch (Exception e) {
   338	            LOG.error("Error processing CBOR request: " + serviceName + "." + action, e);
   339	            return Response.status(500).build();
   340	        }
   341	    }
   342	
   343	    /** Dispatches a CBOR request to the appropriate service handler by SDK service ID. */
   344	    private Response dispatchCbor(String serviceId, String operation, JsonNode request, String region) throws Exception {
   345	        return switch (serviceId) {
   346	            case "DynamoDB" -> dynamoDbJsonHandler.handle(operation, request, region);
   347	            case "DynamoDB Streams" -> dynamoDbStreamsJsonHandler.handle(operation, request, region);
   348	            case "SQS" -> sqsJsonHandler.handle(operation, request, region);
   349	            case "SNS" -> snsJsonHandler.handle(operation, request, region);
   350	            case "SFN" -> sfnJsonHandler.handle(operation, request, region);
   351	            case CLOUDWATCH_SERVICE_ID -> cloudWatchMetricsJsonHandler.handle(operation, request, region);
   352	            default -> null;
   353	        };
   354	    }

The file looks good. Now I need to think about potential conflicts. The S3Controller has:

- `@POST @Path("/{bucket}")` - handles `?delete` and `multipart/form-data`
- `@POST @Path("/{bucket}/{key:.+}")` - handles `?uploads`, `?restore`, `?select`, etc.

With my addition of `@POST @Path("/{accountId}/{queueName}")` in AwsJsonController, there could be ambiguity when a request comes to `/{accountId}/{queueName}` with `Content-Type: application/x-amz-json-1.0`. 

The JAX-RS specification (Section 3.7.2) says:
1. Sort by number of literal characters in the path pattern (more is better)
2. Sort by number of capturing groups (fewer is better)
3. Sort by number of capturing groups with non-default regular expressions (fewer is better)

The S3Controller's `@Path("/{bucket}/{key:.+}")` has a regex pattern `.+` which makes it less specific than `@Path("/{accountId}/{queueName}")` which has default patterns. So `/{accountId}/{queueName}` should be preferred.

But also, the `@Consumes` annotation should help: AwsJsonController's `@Consumes("application/x-amz-json-1.0")` is more specific than no `@Consumes` on S3Controller.

Now, there's one more thing I should consider: the S3Controller also has `@POST @Path("/{bucket}")` (single segment). This could match a path like `/{something}`. But our new handler only matches two segments `/{accountId}/{queueName}`, so it wouldn't conflict with single-segment paths.

Let me also think about whether we need to handle the CBOR case similarly. Looking at the CBOR handler:

```java

@Produces("application/cbor")
public Response handleCborRequest(...)
```

This also only handles root path. But the PR description specifically mentions JSON 1.0. The newer SQS SDK uses JSON 1.0. CBOR is a different protocol (smithy-rpc-v2-cbor) and might have its own path pattern (`service/{sdkId}/operation/{op}`). So I think we're fine.

2026-05-30 06:25:30,206 - INFO - swea-agent-floci-io__floci-153 - 💭 THOUGHT
I don't see any existing tests that test JSON 1.0 requests to the queue URL path. The only JSON test in SqsIntegrationTest sends to `POST /` (root path).

My fix should address the issue described in the PR. Let me now do a final review of the changes and think about edge cases.

One concern: what if there are path segments beyond `/accountId/queueName`? For example, SQS might have some operations that use additional path segments. Let me check the AWS SQS API documentation...

Actually, looking at the AWS SQS REST API, all operations are POST to the queue URL which is `/{accountId}/{queueName}`. There are no additional path segments. The query string parameters are used for the older query protocol, and the JSON protocol uses the request body.

Another concern: what about the `GetQueueAttributes` operation when sent via JSON 1.0 to the queue URL path? The `QueueUrl` parameter in the JSON body contains the full queue URL. But when the request is sent to the queue URL path, the SDK might or might not include the `QueueUrl` in the body. Let me check the SqsJsonHandler to see if it requires `QueueUrl`:

Looking at `handleGetQueueAttributes`:
```java
private Response handleGetQueueAttributes(JsonNode request, String region) {
    String queueUrl = request.path("QueueUrl").asText(null);
    ...
}
```

It reads `QueueUrl` from the request body. If the newer SDK doesn't include `QueueUrl` in the body (because it's implicit from the path), this would fail. But the PR description says the SDK sends the request to `/{accountId}/{queueName}` and the issue is that it's routed to S3Controller. The PR doesn't mention any issue with missing `QueueUrl`. So I assume the SDK still includes `QueueUrl` in the body.

Actually, looking at the Ruby test script in the PR:
```ruby
resp = client.send_message(
    queue_url: queue_url,
    message_body: "hello from ruby",
    message_group_id: "group1",
    message_deduplication_id: "dedup1"
)
```

The Ruby SDK would internally construct the JSON body with the `QueueUrl` parameter and send it to the queue URL path. The JSON body would include `QueueUrl` even though it's also in the path.

So my fix should be sufficient: it catches the request at the correct path and delegates to `dispatchJson` which routes based on `X-Amz-Target` header.

Let me also think about whether I should handle the path parameters (`accountId` and `queueName`) to set up the region correctly. Currently, the `handleJsonRequestWithPath` method extracts `accountId` and `queueName` from the path but doesn't use them. The region is resolved from `regionResolver.resolveRegion(httpHeaders)`. This should be fine because the region can be determined from the `Authorization` header or other headers.

However, there's a potential improvement: if the `QueueUrl` is not provided in the body, we could construct it from the path parameters. But since the SDK includes `QueueUrl` in the body, this isn't necessary. And if it becomes necessary, it would be a separate enhancement.

I think my fix is complete and correct. Let me now submit.

Actually, wait. Let me reconsider the approach. Instead of adding a separate method, maybe I should use a wildcard path pattern to catch all paths. Like:

```java
@POST
@Path("/{path:.*}")
@Consumes("application/x-amz-json-1.0")
```

This would catch any path that starts with `/` and has any number of segments. But this could be too greedy and might catch paths that should be handled by other controllers. The more specific `/{accountId}/{queueName}` is better.

Alternatively, I could keep the class-level `@Path("/")` and add a method like:

```java
@POST
@Path("{accountId}/{queueName}")
```

But since the class already has `@Path("/")`, the resulting path would be `//{accountId}/{queueName}` which normalizes to `/{accountId}/{queueName}`. That's what I did.

Actually, there's another consideration. Looking at the S3Controller, it has `@Path("/")` at class level. The AwsJsonController also has `@Path("/")` at class level. Both have methods that could match `/{accountId}/{queueName}`. 

With my change:
- AwsJsonController: `@POST @Path("/{accountId}/{queueName}") @Consumes("application/x-amz-json-1.0")`
- S3Controller: `@POST @Path("/{bucket}/{key:.+}")` (no `@Consumes`)

The JAX-RS matching algorithm should prefer AwsJsonController for `application/x-amz-json-1.0` requests because it has a more specific `@Consumes`.

But there's a potential issue: what if JAX-RS tries both and picks S3Controller because it was registered first? To be safe, I should also add a guard in S3Controller's POST methods to reject requests with `X-Amz-Target` header.

Let me add that guard:

    @Path("/{bucket}")

    public Response handleBucketPost(@PathParam("bucket") String bucket,
                                      @HeaderParam("Content-Type") String contentType,
                                      @Context UriInfo uriInfo,
                                      byte[] body) {
        try {
            if (hasQueryParam(uriInfo, "delete")) {
                return handleDeleteObjects(bucket, body);
            }
            if (contentType != null && contentType.startsWith("multipart/form-data")) {
                return handlePresignedPost(bucket, contentType, body);
            }
            return xmlErrorResponse(new AwsException("InvalidArgument",
                    "POST on bucket requires ?delete parameter.", 400));
        } catch (AwsException e) {
            return xmlErrorResponse(e);
        }
    }

   585	                                         @PathParam("key") String key,
   586	                                         @QueryParam("uploadId") String uploadId,

   605	                        .elem("Key", key)
   606	                        .elem("UploadId", upload.getUploadId())
   607	                        .end("InitiateMultipartUploadResult")
   608	                        .build();
   609	                return Response.ok(xml).build();
   610	            }
   611

   613	                s3Service.restoreObject(bucket, key, versionId, new String(body, StandardCharsets.UTF_8));
   614	                return Response.accepted().build();
   615	            }

   628	                String baseUrl = uriInfo.getBaseUri().toString();
   629	                if (baseUrl.endsWith("/")) {

1. **AwsJsonController.java**: 
   - Extracted the JSON dispatch logic into a private `dispatchJson` method
   - Added a new endpoint `@POST @Path("/{accountId}/{queueName}")` that also consumes `application/x-amz-json-1.0` and delegates to `dispatchJson`. This handles SQS JSON 1.0 requests sent to the queue URL path (e.g., `/{accountId}/{queueName}`) by newer AWS SDKs.

2. **S3Controller.java**:
   - Added `@HeaderParam("X-Amz-Target") String target` parameter to both `handleBucketPost` and `handleMultipartPost` methods
   - Added early return (`return null`) when `X-Amz-Target` header is present, allowing JAX-RS to fall through to AwsJsonController for JSON protocol requests

These changes ensure that JSON 1.0 requests to `/{accountId}/{queueName}` are properly routed to the SQS handler instead of being caught by the S3Controller.
